This method is used in advanced cases where returning\n   584→   * StopIterationAndBuffer from decodeData() is not sufficient.\n   585→   *\n   586→   * 1) If a headers only request needs to be turned into a request with a body, this method can\n   587→   * be called to add body in the decodeHeaders() callback. Subsequent filters will receive\n   588→   * decodeHeaders(..., false) followed by decodeData(..., true). This works both in the direct\n   589→   * iteration as well as the continuation case.\n   590→   *\n   591→   * 2) If a filter is going to look at all buffered data from within a data callback with end\n   592→   * stream set, this method can be called to immediately buffer the data. This avoids having\n   593→   * to deal with the existing buffered data and the data from the current callback.\n   594→   *\n   595→   * 3) If additional buffered body data needs to be added by a filter before continuation of data\n   596→   * to further filters (outside of callback context).\n   597→   *\n   598→   * 4) If additional data needs to be added in the decodeTrailers() callback, this method can be\n   599→   * called in the context of the callback. All further filters will receive decodeData(..., false)\n   600→   * followed by decodeTrailers(). However if the iteration is stopped, the added data will\n   601→   * buffered, so that the further filters will not receive decodeData() before decodeHeaders().\n   602→   *\n   603→   * It is an error to call this method in any other case.\n   604→   *\n   605→   * See also injectDecodedDataToFilterChain() for a different way of passing data to further\n   606→   * filters and also how the two methods are different.\n   607→   *\n   608→   * @param data Buffer::Instance supplies the data to be decoded.\n   609→   * @param streaming_filter boolean supplies if this filter streams data or buffers the full body.\n   610→   */\n   611→  virtual void addDecodedData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool streaming_filter) PURE;\n   612→\n   613→  /**\n   614→   * Decode data directly to subsequent filters in the filter chain. Using this method allows\n   617→   * a filter to buffer data (or not) and then periodically inject data to subsequent filters,\n   618→   * indicating end_stream at an appropriate time. This can be used to implement rate limiting,\n   619→   * periodic data emission, etc.\n   620→   *\n   621→   * This method should only be called outside of callback context. I.e., do not call this method\n   622→   * from within a filter's decodeData() call.\n   623→   *\n   624→   * When using this callback, filters should generally only return\n   625→   * FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer from their decodeData() call, since use of this method\n   626→   * indicates that a filter does not wish to participate in standard HTTP connection manager\n   627→   * buffering and continuation and will perform any necessary buffering and continuation on its\n   628→   * own.\n   629→   *\n   630→   * This callback is different from addDecodedData() in that the specified data and end_stream\n   631→   * status will be propagated directly to further filters in the filter chain. of several key architectural components:\\n\\n## Filter Factory Registry\\nThe filter factory registry is defined through the `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` interface (envoy/server/filter_config.h) which all HTTP filter factories must implement. The concrete registry managers are implemented in source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h: `HttpFilterConfigProviderManagerImpl` manages downstream HTTP filter configurations and `UpstreamHttpFilterConfigProviderManagerImpl` manages upstream HTTP filter configurations.\\n\\n## Filter Context\\nThe filter context is represented by the `FilterContext` struct (envoy/http/filter_factory.h) which contains the filter configuration name and filter extension name. Additionally, `Server::Configuration::FactoryContext` and `Server::Configuration::UpstreamFactoryContext` provide the broader context for filter creation.\\n\\n## Per-Request Filter Chain Execution\\nThe per-request filter chain execution is orchestrated by:\\n1. `FilterManager` (source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc) - Manages the per-request filter chain state and iteration through filters\\n2. `ConnectionManagerImpl` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc) - Creates new filter chains for each HTTP stream\\n3. `FilterChainFactory` interface and its implementation `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` (source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h/cc) -
